Final Refutation: Why Two Independent Causes Are Possible
Concludes that the proof against two independent causes fails.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the argument against a single effect having two independent causes is invalid.

Core Idea
The need for a cause in general does not conflict with multiple specific causes.

This final passage presents the conclusive refutation of the earlier impossibility proof. The author argues that if dependence on a particular cause arises from that cause's requirement, then a single effect can be caused by two independent causes without needing either specifically. Thus, the combination does not lead to contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Understand the premise
The passage starts with a conditional: if dependence on a particular cause arises from its requirement, then a single individual can have two independent causes. Recognize that the effect is not in need of anything specific from them.
2
Analyze the implication
The combination of two causes would not make the effect both in need and independent with respect to each; rather, it is in need of some cause, not each specifically.
3
See the conclusion
The need for a cause in general does not contradict having two specific causes because independence is from the specificity, not from the general concept.
4
Apply the lesson
The proof against two independent causes is therefore not established. Avoid following misguided opinions on this topic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أنه لما جاز أن يكون الاستناد إلى علة معينة ناشئاً من اقتضاء العلة المعينة دون احتياج المعلول إلى تلك العلة المعينة جاز أن يكون الواحد الشخص معللا بعلتين مستقلتين، ولا يكون محتاجاً إلى شيء منهما بعينه، حتى يلزم من اجتماعهما كونه محتاجاً ومستغنياً بالقياس إلى كل واحدة منهما، بل يكون محتاجاً إلى علة ما . وهذا الاحتياج لا ينافي الاجتماع؛ لأنهما إذا اجتمعتا لزم الاستغناء عن خصوصية كل منهما، لا عن مفهوم أحدهما الذي هو أعم منهما ، فلا يتم الدليل المعول عليه في امتناع تعليل الواحد الشخصي بعلل مستقلة وقد خبط في تقرير هذا المقام أقوام فلا تتبع أهواءهم بعد ما جاءك من الحق.
Because when it is allowed that the dependence on a particular cause arises from the requirement of the particular cause without the effect's need for that particular cause, it is allowed that the one person be caused by two independent causes, and he is not in need of anything specifically from them, such that from their combination there would follow him being in need and independent with respect to each of them. Rather, he is in need of some cause. And this need does not contradict their combination because when they combine, independence from the specificity of each follows, not from the concept of one of them which is more general than both. So the proof relied upon for the impossibility of causing a single individual by independent causes is not established. And people have stumbled in the exposition of this topic, so do not follow their desires after what has come to you of the truth.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage presents the conclusive argument that the original impossibility proof fails. It argues that if dependence on a particular cause arises from the cause's requirement, then a single effect can have two independent causes without needing either specifically. Thus, when they combine, the effect is independent of their specific characteristics but still needs a cause in general. The need for a general cause does not conflict with having two specific causes. Therefore, the proof that a single individual cannot have multiple independent causes is invalid. The author warns against following misguided opinions on this.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The combination of two independent causes would make the effect both in need and independent of each.
Correction: Actually, the effect is independent of the specificity of each but still needs a cause in general, which is not contradictory.

Key Takeaway

What would it mean for your worship and gratitude if you truly believed that Allah can bring about a single outcome through multiple independent causes without contradiction?
?
This lesson demonstrates that the need for a cause in general does not conflict with having multiple specific causes. Is there a situation in your life where you have felt torn between two possible paths or influences, thinking you must choose one as the 'real' cause? How does this insight free you to see that Allah can work through both—and that your need is ultimately for Him alone?
